This class runs a consumer in a background thread to continuously tail the target\n69:  *     topic, accepts write requests which it writes to the topic using an internal producer, and provides some helpful\n70:  *     utilities like checking the current log end offset and waiting until the current end of the log is reached.\n71:  * </p>\n72:  * <p>\n73:  *     To support different use cases, this class works with either single- or multi-partition topics.\n74:  * </p>\n75:  * <p>\n76:  *     Since this class is generic, it delegates the details of data storage via a callback that is invoked for each\n77:  *     record that is consumed from the topic. In such cases, using 'consumer.endOffsets(...)' will block until at least\n504:         // one more record becomes available, meaning we can't even check whether we're at the end offset.\n505:         // Since all we're trying to do here is get the end offset, we should use the supplied admin client\n506:         // (if available) to obtain the end offsets for the given topic partitions.\n507: \n508:         // Deprecated constructors do not provide an admin supplier, so the admin is potentially null.\n509:         if (admin != null) {\n510:             // Use the admin client to }\n518: \n519:                 return admin.endOffsets(assignment);\n520:             } catch (UnsupportedVersionException e) {\n521:                 // This may happen with really old brokers that don't support the auto topic creation\n522:                 // field in metadata requests\n523:                 if (requireAdminForOffsets) {\n524:                     // Should be handled by the caller during log startup\n525:                     throw e;\n526:                 }\n527:                 log.debug(\"Reading to end of log offsets with consumer since admin client is unsupported:
